      '\r\n' +

      '\r\n' +
      'Since commit 78524b05f1a3 ("mm, swap avoid redundant swap device\r\n' +
      'pinning"), the common helper for allocating and preparing a folio in the\r\n' +
      'swap cache layer no longer tries to get a swap device reference\r\n' +
      'internally, because all callers of __read_swap_cache_async are already\r\n' +
      "holding a swap entry reference.  The repeated swap device pinning isn't\r\n" +
      'needed on the same swap device.\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      "Caller of VMA readahead is also holding a reference to the target entry's\r\n" +
      'swap device, but VMA readahead walks the page table, so it might encounter\r\n' +
      'swap entries from other devices, and call __read_swap_cache_async on\r\n' +
      'another device without holding a reference to it.\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      'So it is possible to cause a UAF when swapoff of device A raced with\r\n' +
      'swapin on device B, and VMA readahead tries to read swap entries from\r\n' +
      "device A.  It's not easy to trigger, but in theory, it could cause real\r\n" +
      'issues.\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +

      'to EMPTY, which may result in uaf access.  We should use RB_CLEAR_NODE()\r\n' +

      '   pde is tun3\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      '2) in the [time windows] unregister netdevice tun3 and tun2, and erase\r\n' +
      '   them from rbtree.  erase tun3 first, and then erase tun2.  the\r\n' +
      '   pde(tun2) will be released to slab\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      '3) continue to getdent process, then pde_subdir_next() will return\r\n' +
      '   pde(tun2) which is released, it will case uaf access.\r\n' +

      '        pde_put(de)                       |\r\n' +
      '        de = next    //UAF                |\r\n' +

      '\r\n' +
      'mm/secretmem fix use-after-free race in fault handler\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      'When a page fault occurs in a secret memory file created with\r\n' +
      '`memfd_secret(2)`, the kernel will allocate a new folio for it, mark the\r\n' +

      '\r\n' +
      'If two tasks cause a fault in the same page concurrently, both could end\r\n' +
      'up allocating a folio and removing the page from the direct map, but only\r\n' +
      'one would succeed in adding the folio to the file mapping.  The task that\r\n' +
      'failed undoes the effects of its attempt by (a) freeing the folio again\r\n' +
      'and (b) putting the page back into the direct map.  However, by doing\r\n' +
      'these two operations in this order, the page becomes available to the\r\n' +
      'allocator again before it is placed back in the direct mapping.\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +

      'kernel tries to access it via the direct map, it would result in a\r\n' +
      'supervisor not-present page fault.\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      'Fix the ordering to restore the direct map before the folio is freed. | Severity UNKNOWN  ]]>]]>]]>]]>]]>]]>]]>]]>]]>]]>]]>]]>]]>]]>]]>]]>]]>',

      '\r\n' +

    link: 'https//nvd.nist.gov/vuln/detail/CVE-2025-40288',

    content: '![CDATA[![CDATA[![CDATA[![CDATA[![CDATA[![CDATA[![CDATA[![CDATA[![CDATA[![CDATA[![CDATA[![CDATA[![CDATA[![CDATA[![CDATA[![CDATA[![CDATA[In the Linux kernel, the following vulnerability has been resolved\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      'drm/amdgpu Fix NULL pointer dereference in VRAM logic for APU devices\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      'Previously, APU platforms (and other scenarios with uninitialized VRAM managers)\r\n' +
      'triggered a NULL pointer dereference in `ttm_resource_manager_usage()`. The root\r\n' +
      'cause is not that the `struct ttm_resource_manager *man` pointer itself is NULL,\r\n' +
      'but that `man->bdev` (the backing device pointer within the manager) remains\r\n' +
      'uninitialized (NULL) on APUs—since APUs lack dedicated VRAM and do not fully\r\n' +
      'set up VRAM manager structures. When `ttm_resource_manager_usage()` attempts to\r\n' +
      'acquire `man->bdev->lru_lock`, it dereferences the NULL `man->bdev`, leading to\r\n' +
      'a kernel OOPS.\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      '1. **amdgpu_cs.c** Extend the existing bandwidth control check in\r\n' +
      '   `amdgpu_cs_get_threshold_for_moves()` to include a check for\r\n' +
      '   `ttm_resource_manager_used()`. If the manager is not used (uninitialized\r\n' +
      '   `bdev`), return 0 for migration thresholds immediately—skipping VRAM-specific\r\n' +
      '   logic that would trigger the NULL dereference.\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      '2. **amdgpu_kms.c** Update the `AMDGPU_INFO_VRAM_USAGE` ioctl and memory info\r\n' +
      '   reporting to use a conditional if the manager is used, return the real VRAM\r\n' +
      '   usage otherwise, return 0. This avoids accessing `man->bdev` when it is\r\n' +
      '   NULL.\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      '3. **amdgpu_virt.c** Modify the vf2pf (virtual function to physical function)\r\n' +
      '   data write path. Use `ttm_resource_manager_used()` to check validity if the\r\n' +
      '   manager is usable, calculate `fb_usage` from VRAM usage otherwise, set\r\n' +
      '   `fb_usage` to 0 (APUs have no discrete framebuffer to report).\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      'This approach is more robust than APU-specific checks because it\r\n' +
      '- Works for all scenarios where the VRAM manager is uninitialized (not just APUs),\r\n' +
      "- Aligns with TTM's design by using its native helper function,\r\n" +
      '- Preserves correct behavior for discrete GPUs (which have fully initialized\r\n' +
      '  `man->bdev` and pass the `ttm_resource_manager_used()` check).\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
